<li id="cite_note-Christian-171"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Christian_171-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Customary in some Coptic and other churches:
<ul><li>"The Coptic Christians in Egypt and the Ethiopian Orthodox Christians— two of the oldest surviving forms of Christianity— retain many of the features of early Christianity, including male circumcision. Circumcision is not prescribed in other forms of Christianity... Some Christian churches in South Africa oppose the practice, viewing it as a pagan ritual, while others, including the Nomiya church in Kenya, require circumcision for membership and participants in focus group discussions in Zambia and Malawi mentioned similar beliefs that Christians should practice circumcision since Jesus was circumcised and the Bible teaches the practice."</li>
<li>"The decision that Christians need not practice circumcision is recorded in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://bible.oremus.org/?passage=Acts+15–15&amp;version=nrsv">Acts 15</a>; there was never, however, a prohibition of circumcision, and it is practiced by Coptic Christians." <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20080720054046/http://bartleby.com/65/ci/circumci.html">"circumcision"</a>, The Columbia Encyclopedia, Sixth Edition, 2001–05.</li></ul>
</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-WrightVilaça2013-172"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-WrightVilaça2013_172-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Wright, Professor Robin M; Vilaça, Aparecida (28 May 2013). <i>Native Christians: Modes and Effects of Christianity among Indigenous Peoples of the Americas</i>. <li id="cite_note-Geisler1989-173"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Geisler1989_173-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Geisler, Norman L. (1 September 1989). <i>Christian Ethics: Contemporary Issues and Options</i>. Baker Books. p.&#160;334. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-58558-053-8" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-58558-053-8"><bdi>978-1-58558-053-8</bdi></a>. <q><i>The eating of animals is not forbidden.</i> The Scriptures do not forbid the eating and partaking of animals. This does not mean that all animals are to be eaten (Mark 7:19; Acts 11:9; 1 Tim. 4:4). It is clear in the Scriptures that we are not supposed to eat animals that are alive or with blood (Gen. 9:2–4; Deut. 12:16, 23–24).</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Christian+Ethics%3A+Contemporary+Issues+and+Options&amp;rft.pages=334&amp;rft.pub=Baker+Books&amp;rft.date=1989-09-01&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-58558-053-8&amp;rft.aulast=Geisler&amp;rft.aufirst=Norman+L.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+culture" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-Ehrman2006-174"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Ehrman2006_174-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Ehrman, Bart D. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2 May</span> 2014</span>. <q>In the meantime, Peter in Joppa has a middday vision in which he sees a sheet containing animals of every description lowered from the sky. But then he hears a voice that tells him, "What God has cleansed, you must not call common [unclean]" (that is, you do not need to refrain from eating nonkosher foods; 10: 15). The same sequence of events happens three times.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Peter%2C+Paul%2C+and+Mary+Magdalene%3A+The+Followers+of+Jesus+in+History+and+Legend&amp;rft.pages=60&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2006-05-01&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-19-974113-7&amp;rft.aulast=Ehrman&amp;rft.aufirst=Bart+D.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DTlvgp7WggvEC%26pg%3DPA60&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChristian+culture" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-175"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-175">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">"The Weaker Brother". <i>Third Way Magazine</i>. <b>25</b> (10): 25. <li id="cite_note-Deem-177"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Deem_177-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Deem, Rich (21 June 2008). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.godandscience.org/doctrine/vegetarian.html">"Should Christians Eat Meat or Should We Be Vegetarians?"</a>. <li id="cite_note-Anglican_Catholic-186"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Anglican_Catholic_186-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Barrows, Susanna; Room, Robin (1991). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=o-wmSdtGer0C&amp;pg=PA340"><i>Drinking: Behavior and Belief in Modern History</i></a>. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2 May</span> 2014</span>. <q>The main legally enforced prohibition in both Catholic and Anglican countries was that against meat.
